With this facial hair remover, I was able to easily remove my facial hair with minimal pain.<br /><br />After ordering, this product arrived two days later. After removing it from the packaging, you see the the long spiral coil with two handles on either end. To use this facial hair remover, you hold the coil against your skin, stretch it apart, let the coil fold back into themselves and pull the coil away from your face. When you look down at the coil, you see the hairs between the coils. Simply stretching the coils back apart empties the hair from the coils. Then, you are able to start again.<br /><br />Despite the fact that you are basically plucking a lot of the hair out at one time, I found this to not be very painful. This quite surprised me honestly. Even plucking my eyebrows will make my eyes water. This felt almost like my skin was being pinched. Okay, they did a good job but they could also burned the skin if not careful. Waxing--Hot wax. Oh yes, I had my share of a scabstache, you know when the hot wax is ripped off and takes some of the skin! Cold wax--didn't grab the skin as well as the hot nor did it pull out the fine hairs. These were all through my teen years.<br /><br />Now into my late teens and early adult years. I tried one of those sand paper like hair removal stuff. Never worked on me, it exfoliated my skin and in certain spots on the face made it more sensitive. Hair removal was minimal and it took major time doing it. Threading--not coordinated enough and still not today! Epilators--Yes, this has been my go-to product for my adult life! I have been using the Braun and it has been good. Only 2 problems: uses up batteries like crazy. 4 AAA batteries lose their steam after a couple of uses which cost a lot! Another major drawback, it doesn't catch the really fine hairs.<br /><br />Okay, now for the BELLABE. No way! Can't work! Too simple of a gadget!<br /><br />Well, my skepticism turned to belief! First if you never have done any facial removal, you will feel sensitivity. Here are a few things you need to do BEFORE you use it.<br /><br />Your skin has to be clean of any oils or the coil won't catch the hair. You should swipe the area of hair removal with rubbing alcohol and also spritz some on the coils. If you feel pain or sensitivity when using the product, I suggest getting some Anbesol and applying onto the area used. This will numb the area just enough for the hair removal.<br /><br />Once you have prepped the skin, you have to learn how to use it. First hold the handles between your fingers and bend into a &#34;U&#34; shape. Next, roll THE HANDLES between your fingers and just move the coil up and down the area of hair removal. THAT'S IT! When you are finished, just spritz the Bellabe with alcohol to keep it clean and oil free and store in the given container.<br /><br />What I couldn't believe is that it removed all of the hair including the baby fine ones which my epilator never removed or couldn't remove. Another thing is, I don't need batteries which makes it perfect for traveling. It is a quiet little tool that actually removes the facial hair effectively. I won't go back to my Braun, Bellabe is it for me from now on!

  648. I almost never write reviews, but after using my new Bellabe for the first time today, I have to rate it FIVE STARS! I am a post-menopausal woman who has plenty of long, blonde, silky hair -- too bad it's all over my face and neck. Along with a few dark and brittle ones that pop up on the chin and moustache. Yuuuuuuck. I've paid for professional full-face waxing which is inconvenient, expensive and painful -- my skin is sensitive and I've had minor burns from wax that was too hot. I switched to depilatory cream every two weeks for the past couple of years, until three weeks ago, when the stuff burned my face so badly I looked like a meth addict. I was in despair when I went online and started researching. Bellabe sounded like a dream come true, and, feeling optimistic, I ordered the two-pack. Ladies, you won't believe this thing!!! I was worried because if it didn't work, I didn't know what I was going to do about the facial hair. Plus, I am usually a total klutz with tools of any kind. It took less than five minutes for me to figure it out and get the feel for it! I watched a video from Youtube first, which helped, because frankly, the package directions weren't very good. Once I got the hang of it, it was actually fun ... I know, I know, how fun can it be to rip your unwanted hair out by the roots? But it was strangely addictive, like popping those plastic bubbles on shipping wrap. The best part of all -- I was done in less than 15 minutes and my face and neck feels totally smooth and soft. I had minimal redness which disappeared in less than 20 minutes. The Bellabe grabbed all the hairs except for the very shortest, finest ones, which gives a much more natural appearance. It looks like I have natural &#34;peach fuzz&#34; like I had before menopause. I will never be without this tool again. Here are a few tips that they don't mention in the directions: 1. The handles are printed with a number 1 on one end and a number 2 on the other. I had no idea why, so I experimented and found out that the tool works if you hold the 1 in your left hand and the 2 in your right hand, and twist the handles inward (fingers toward each other, toward the center of the inverted U shape.) 2. Be certain to twist each handle at the same time, firmly, as you roll it against the direction of hair growth. When it's working, you'll feel and see it gently grab all the hairs it can, slightly pulling your skin up as it goes. 3. It helps to puff up your face anywhere you can to make it more taut; the spring grabs the hair better that way. It's not nearly as painful as waxing, for some reason (the only exception being the middle of the upper lip -- that was pretty intense). But that is the only negative thing I have to say, and we all pay a price for beauty, right? I promise you will love it!

Put it in perspective folks. Once you get the \\"hang\\" of twirling the handles in your little fingers to produce the torqueing action of the spring enough to actually pull hairs, it's a breeze. For the \\"tougher hairs\\" don't curve the spring so much, level it out a little, twirl, then bend. Might take a few tries, or just resort to the Medieval tweezer method for the die hard hairs. My only words of caution would be... do NOT use this on eyebrows. My tips are: Get a clean, unused toothbrush. Take one end of the Bellabe between your teeth and pull the Bellabe slightly with the other hand to stretch it out only slightly. With the remaining hand, take the clean toothbrush and brush the spring out on all sides. Clean the toothbrush with alcohol or whatever, and allow to dry for the next cleaning.
